ns-0 ns-subject page-List_of_islands_of_Scotland rootpage-List_of_islands_of_Scotland skin-vector action-view">\t\t<div id="mw-page-base" class="noprint"></div>\n\t\t<div id="mw-head-base" class="noprint"></div>\n\t\t<div id="content" class="mw-body" role="main">\n\t\t\t<a id="top"></a>\n\t\t\t<div id="siteNotice" class="mw-body-content"><!-- CentralNotice --></div><div class="mw-indicators mw-body-content">\n<div id="mw-indicator-featured-star" class="mw-indicator"><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Featured_lists" title="This is a featured list. Click here for more information."><img alt="This is a featured list. Click here for more information." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e7/Cscr-featured.svg/20px-Cscr-featured.svg.png" width="20" height="19" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e7/Cscr-featured.svg/30px-Cscr-featured.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e7/Cscr-featured.svg/40px-Cscr-featured.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="462" data-file-height="438" /></a></div>\n</div>\n<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">List of islands of Scotland</h1>\t\t\t<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">\n\t\t\t\t<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>\t\t\t\t<div id="contentSub"></div>\n\t\t\t\t<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>\t\t\t\t<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>\n\t\t\t\t<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>\n\t\t\t\t<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:277px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hebridesmap.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Hebridesmap.png/275px-Hebridesmap.png" width="275" height="426" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Hebridesmap.png/413px-Hebridesmap.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Hebridesmap.png/550px-Hebridesmap.png 2x" data-file-width="935" data-file-height="1450" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hebridesmap.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of the Inner and Outer <a href="/wiki/Hebrides" title="Hebrides">Hebrides</a></div></div></div>\n<p>This is a <b>list of islands of Scotland</b>, the mainland of which is part of the island of <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain" title="Great Britain">Great Britain</a>. Also included are various other related tables and lists. The definition of an offshore <a href="/wiki/Island" title="Island">island</a> used in this list is "land that is surrounded by seawater on a daily basis, but not necessarily at all stages of the tide, excluding human devices such as bridges and causeways".<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;Note 1&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a> has over 790 offshore islands, most of which are to be found in four main groups: <a href="/wiki/Shetland_Islands" class="mw-redirect" title="Shetland Islands">Shetland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Orkney_Islands" class="mw-redirect" title="Orkney Islands">Orkney</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Hebrides" title="Hebrides">Hebrides</a>, sub-divided into the <a href="/wiki/Inner_Hebrides" title="Inner Hebrides">Inner Hebrides</a> and <a href="/wiki/Outer_Hebrides" title="Outer Hebrides">Outer Hebrides</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Smith_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Smith-2">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> There are also clusters of islands in the <a href="/wiki/Firth_of_Clyde" title="Firth of Clyde">Firth of Clyde</a>, <a href="/wiki/Firth_of_Forth" title="Firth of Forth">Firth of Forth</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Solway_Firth" title="Solway Firth">Solway Firth</a>, and numerous small islands within the many bodies of <a href="/wiki/Freshwater" class="mw-redirect" title="Freshwater">fresh water</a> in Scotland including <a href="/wiki/Loch_Lomond" title="Loch Lomond">Loch Lomond</a> and <a href="/wiki/Loch_Maree" title="Loch Maree">Loch Maree</a>. The largest island is <a href="/wiki/Lewis_and_Harris" title="Lewis and Harris">Lewis and Harris</a> which extends to 2,179&#160;square kilometres, and there are a further 200 islands which are greater than 40&#160;<a href="/wiki/Hectares" class="mw-redirect" title="Hectares">hectares</a> in area. Of the remainder, several such as <a href="/wiki/Staffa" title="Staffa">Staffa</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Flannan_Isles" title="Flannan Isles">Flannan Isles</a> are well known despite their small size.<sup id="cite_ref-Smith_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Smith-2">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> Some 94 Scottish islands are permanently inhabited, of which 89 are offshore islands. Between 2001 and 2011 Scottish island populations as a whole grew by 4% to 103,702.<sup id="cite_ref-BBCr_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCr-3">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The geology and geomorphology of the islands is varied. Some, such as <a href="/wiki/Skye" title="Skye">Skye</a> and <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Mull" class="mw-redirect" title="Isle of Mull">Mull</a> are mountainous, while others like <a href="/wiki/Tiree" title="Tiree">Tiree</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sanday,_Orkney" title="Sanday, Orkney">Sanday</a> are relatively low lying. Many have bedrock made from ancient <a href="/wiki/Archean" title="Archean">Archaean</a> <a href="/wiki/Lewisian_complex" title="Lewisian complex">Lewisian Gneiss</a> which was formed 3 billion years ago; <a href="/wiki/Shapinsay" title="Shapinsay">Shapinsay</a> and other Orkney islands are formed from <a href="/wiki/Old_Red_Sandstone" title="Old Red Sandstone">Old Red Sandstone</a>, which is 400 million years old; and others such as <a href="/wiki/R%C3%B9m" title="R\xc3\xb9m">R\xc3\xb9m</a> from more recent <a href="/wiki/Tertiary" title="Tertiary">Tertiary</a> <a href="/wiki/Volcanoes" class="mw-redirect" title="Volcanoes">volcanoes</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> Many of the islands are swept by strong tides, and the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Corryvreckan" title="Gulf of Corryvreckan">Corryvreckan tide race</a> between <a href="/wiki/Scarba" title="Scarba">Scarba</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jura,_Scotland" title="Jura, Scotland">Jura</a> is one of the largest whirlpools in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> Other strong tides are to be found in the <a href="/wiki/Pentland_Firth" title="Pentland Firth">Pentland Firth</a> between mainland Scotland and <a href="/wiki/Orkney" title="Orkney">Orkney</a>, and another example is the "Grey Dog" between Scarba and <a href="/wiki/Lunga,_Firth_of_Lorn" class="mw-redirect" title="Lunga, Firth of Lorn">Lunga</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Smith_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Smith-2">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The culture of the islands has been affected by the successive influences of <a href="/wiki/Celtic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Celtic language">Celtic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Old_Norse_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Old Norse language">Norse</a> and <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a> speaking peoples and this is reflected in names given to the islands. Most of the <a href="/wiki/Hebrides" title="Hebrides">Hebrides</a> have names with <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Gaelic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Scottish Gaelic language">Scots Gaelic</a> derivations, whilst those of the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Isles" title="Northern Isles">Northern Isles</a> tend to be derived from the <a href="/wiki/Viking" class="mw-redirect" title="Viking">Viking</a> names. A few have <a href="/wiki/Britons_(historical)" class="mw-redirect" title="Britons (historical)">Brythonic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scots_language" title="Scots language">Scots</a> and even perhaps pre-Celtic roots.<sup id="cite_ref-Smith_2-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Smith-2">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>\nA feature of modern island life is the low crime rate and they are considered to be amongst the safest places to live in <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">Britain</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> Orkney was rated as the best place to live in Scotland in both 2013 and 2014 according to the Halifax Quality of Life survey.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Rockall" title="Rockall">Rockall</a> is a small rocky islet in the North Atlantic which was declared part of Scotland by the <a href="/wiki/Island_of_Rockall_Act_1972" title="Island of Rockall Act 1972">Island of Rockall Act 1972</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> However, despite no possession by any other state and other precedents, the legality of the claim is disputed by the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland" title="Republic of Ireland">Republic of Ireland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Denmark" title="Denmark">Denmark</a> and <a href="/wiki/Iceland" title="Iceland">Iceland</a> and some say, it may be unenforceable in international law.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Eilean_Donan_castle_-_95mm.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Eilean_Donan_castle_-_95mm.jpg/220px-Eilean_Donan_castle_-_95mm.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Eilean_Donan_castle_-_95mm.jpg/330px-Eilean_Donan_castle_-_95mm.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Eilean_Donan_castle_-_95mm.jpg/440px-Eilean_Donan_castle_-_95mm.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4188" data-file-height="2792" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Eilean_Donan_castle_-_95mm.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Eilean_Donan" title="Eilean Donan">Eilean Donan</a> castle</div></div></div>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_islands_of_Scotland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Vuiamor2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Vuiamor2.jpg/220px-Vuiamor2.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Vuiamor2.jpg/330px-Vuiamor2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Vuiamor2.jpg/440px-Vuiamor2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="428" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Vuiamor2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Abandoned houses on <a href="/wiki/Fuaigh_M%C3%B2r" title="Fuaigh M\xc3\xb2r">Fuaigh M\xc3\xb2r</a>, which had a population of 46 prior to being <a href="/wiki/Highland_Clearances" title="Highland Clearances">cleared</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_Census_2011" class="mw-redirect" title="United Kingdom Census 2011">2011 census</a> records 94 Scottish islands as having a usually resident population of which 89 are offshore islands. There are however various complications with both the definitions of an "island" and occasional habitation and the <a href="/wiki/National_Records_of_Scotland" title="National Records of Scotland">National Records of Scotland</a> also list a further 17 islands that were inhabited in 2001 but not 2011, or are "included in the NRS statistical geography for inhabited islands but had no usual residents at the time of either the 2001 or 2011 censuses".<sup id="cite_ref-NRS_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NRS-13">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> There are a small number of other islands that are evidently inhabited but which are not recorded in this list.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;Note 2&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Local_government_in_Scotland" title="Local government in Scotland">local government</a> <a href="/wiki/Council_areas_of_Scotland" class="mw-redirect" title="Council areas of Scotland">council areas</a> with the most inhabited islands are <a href="/wiki/Argyll_and_Bute" title="Argyll and Bute">Argyll and Bute</a> with 23, Orkney with 20, Shetland with 16 and <a href="/wiki/Highland_(council_area)" title="Highland (council area)">Highland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Comhairle_nan_Eilean_Siar" title="Comhairle nan Eilean Siar">Comhairle nan Eilean Siar</a> with 14 each. There are also  three in <a href="/wiki/North_Ayrshire" title="North Ayrshire">North Ayrshire</a> and one each in <a href="/wiki/Fife" title="Fife">Fife</a>, <a href="/wiki/Perth_and_Kinross" title="Perth and Kinross">Perth and Kinross</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stirling_(council_area)" title="Stirling (council area)">Stirling</a> and <a href="/wiki/West_Dunbartonshire" title="West Dunbartonshire">West Dunbartonshire</a>. The last three named plus two islands in Argyll and Bute are freshwater rather than offshore.<sup id="cite_ref-NRS_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NRS-13">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Portree_(2477763387).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Portree_%282477763387%29.jpg/220px-Portree_%282477763387%29.jpg" width="220" height="164" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Portree_%282477763387%29.jpg/330px-Portree_%282477763387%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Portree_%282477763387%29.jpg/440px-Portree_%282477763387%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2029" data-file-height="1511" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Portree_(2477763387).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Portree" title="Portree">Portree</a> on <a href="/wiki/Skye" title="Skye">Skye</a>, an island where the population has grown in recent decades.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p>In the past many smaller islands that are  uninhabited today had permanent populations. Losses were severe in many areas during the 19th century when islands such as <a href="/wiki/Pabbay,_Harris" title="Pabbay, Harris">Pabbay</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fuaigh_M%C3%B2r" title="Fuaigh M\xc3\xb2r">Fuaigh M\xc3\xb2r</a> were subject to forcible evictions during the <a href="/wiki/Highland_Clearances" title="Highland Clearances">Highland Clearances</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> Mass emigration from the Hebridean islands was at its height in the mid-19th century but it commenced as early as the 1770s in some areas.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Crofting_counties" class="mw-redirect" title="Crofting counties">crofting counties</a> held 20% of Scotland\'s population in 1755 but by 1961 this figure had declined to 5%.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> Other examples include <a href="/wiki/Mingulay" title="Mingulay">Mingulay</a>, <a href="/wiki/Noss" title="Noss">Noss</a> and the <a href="/wiki/St_Kilda,_Scotland" title="St Kilda, Scotland">St Kilda</a> archipelago, which were abandoned during the course of the 20th century. Declines have been particularly significant in the more remote outlying islands, some of which remain vulnerable to ongoing losses.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The following table shows population trends for the ten most populous islands as of the last census. The overall trends are typically growth in populations in the early part of the modern period, followed by declines from the mid 19th century onwards. In every case except Orkney the highest population was recorded prior to 1932 and the lowest post-<a href="/wiki/Industrial_revolution" class="mw-redirect" title="Industrial revolution">industrial revolution</a> figure after 1960. Subsequently, there has been modest growth overall, although some islands are continuing to show a decline. Between 1991 and 2001, the population of the islands as a whole fell by 3% to 99,739, although there were 35 islands whose population increased.<sup id="cite_ref-GRO_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GRO-20">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> By contrast, between 2001 and 2011 Scottish island populations as a whole grew by 4% to 103,702.<sup id="cite_ref-BBCr_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCr-3">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Local_People_Leading" title="Local People Leading">Scottish Community Alliance</a> noted that "the largest rate of increase has been in the Western Isles (6%) where local people now own approximately 60% of the landmass. Where populations have fallen (Bute, Arran and Islay) community ownership is virtually non-existent."<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Largest_Scottish_islands_by_population">Largest Scottish islands by population</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_islands_of_Scotland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Largest Scottish islands by population">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="wikitable sortable">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th rowspan="2"><b>Rank</b>\n</th>\n<th class="mw-headline" id="Legislation">Legislation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_islands_of_Scotland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Legislation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>In July 2013, the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Government" title="Scottish Government">Scottish Government</a> made the <a href="/wiki/Lerwick_Declaration" title="Lerwick Declaration">Lerwick Declaration</a>, indicating an intention to decentralise power to the three island council areas of Orkney, Shetland and the Western Isles and later that year made a commitment to do so.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> In 2017 an Islands <a href="/wiki/Bill_(law)" title="Bill (law)">bill</a> was introduced to make "island proofing" (including for uninhabited islands) a statutory requirement for public bodies. The Bill completed Stage 1 on 8 February 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Larger_islands">Larger islands</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_islands_of_Scotland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Larger islands">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>This is a list of Scottish islands that either have an area greater than 40&#160;hectares (approximately 100&#160;acres) and/or are inhabited. The main groups, from Haswell-Smith (2004), in many cases provide a more useful guide to location than local authority areas. These groups are: <a href="/wiki/Firth_of_Clyde" title="Firth of Clyde">Firth of Clyde</a>, <a href="/wiki/Islay" title="Islay">Islay</a>, <a href="/wiki/Firth_of_Lorn" title="Firth of Lorn">Firth of Lorn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Mull" class="mw-redirect" title="Isle of Mull">Mull</a>, <a href="/wiki/Small_Isles" title="Small Isles">Small Isles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Skye" title="Skye">Skye</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lewis_and_Harris" title="Lewis and Harris">Lewis and Harris</a>, <a href="/wiki/Uist" title="Uist">Uists</a> and <a href="/wiki/Barra" title="Barra">Barra</a>, <a href="/wiki/St_Kilda,_Scotland" title="St Kilda, Scotland">St Kilda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Orkney" title="Orkney">Orkney</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shetland" title="Shetland">Shetland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Firth_of_Forth" title="Firth of Forth">Firth of Forth</a>. In a few cases where the island is part of either a recognisable smaller group or an archipelago, or is located away from the main groups, an archipelago, local authority or other descriptive name is used instead. "F" designates a freshwater island.\n</p><p>Scotland\'s islands include thirteen <a href="/wiki/Munro" title="Munro">Munros</a> (mountains with a height over 3,000&#160;feet or 914.4&#160;metres), twelve of them found on Skye, and a total of 227 <a href="/wiki/Marilyn_(hill)" class="mw-redirect" title="Marilyn (hill)">Marilyns</a> (hills with a <a href="/wiki/Topographic_prominence" title="Topographic prominence">relative height</a> of at least 150&#160;metres, regardless of <a href="/wiki/Elevation" title="Elevation">absolute height</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-Munros_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Munros-41">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Orkney_Islands.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Orkney_Islands.jpg/200px-Orkney_Islands.jpg" width="200" height="232" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Orkney_Islands.jpg/300px-Orkney_Islands.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Orkney_Islands.jpg/400px-Orkney_Islands.jpg 2x" data-file-width="859" data-file-height="996" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Orkney_Islands.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Orkney aerial photomap</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wfm_shetland_map.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Wfm_shetland_map.png/200px-Wfm_shetland_map.png" width="200" height="262" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Wfm_shetland_map.png/300px-Wfm_shetland_map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Wfm_shetland_map.png/400px-Wfm_shetland_map.png 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="2624" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wfm_shetland_map.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Shetland" title="Shetland">Shetland</a> archipelago</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kirkabister_Ness.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" href="/wiki/Orkney" title="Orkney">Orkney</a>\n</td>\n<td><span style="display:none" class="sortkey">7002311000000000000\xe2\x99\xa0</span>311\n</td>\n<td>29\n</td>\n<td>32\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Yell_(island)" class="mw-redirect" title="Yell (island)">Yell</a>\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Shetland" title="Shetland">Shetland</a>\n</td>\n<td><span style="display:none" class="sortkey">7004212110000000000\xe2\x99\xa0</span>21,211\n</td>\n<td>966\n</td>\n<td>205\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>Four islands were recorded as inhabited in 2011 that were not mentioned in the 2001 census: Eilean d\xc3\xa0 Mh\xc3\xa8inn, Eilean Tioram, Holm of Grimbister and Inner Holm.<sup id="cite_ref-NRS_13-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NRS-13">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>These following are listed by the National Records of Scotland as "included in the NRS statistical geography for inhabited islands but had no usual residents at the time of either the 2001 or 2011 censuses."<sup id="cite_ref-NRS_13-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NRS-13">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> None except Lamb Holm are greater than 40 ha in area.\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable sortable">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th><i><b>Island</b></i>\n</th>\n<th><i><b>Location</b></i>\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Castle_Stalker" title="Castle href="/wiki/Orkney" title="Orkney">Orkney</a>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Freshwater_islands">Freshwater islands</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_islands_of_Scotland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Freshwater islands">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:LochLomond(wfmillar)Jan2000.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/LochLomond%28wfmillar%29Jan2000.jpg/220px-LochLomond%28wfmillar%29Jan2000.jpg" width="220" height="152" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/LochLomond%28wfmillar%29Jan2000.jpg/330px-LochLomond%28wfmillar%29Jan2000.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/LochLomond%28wfmillar%29Jan2000.jpg/440px-LochLomond%28wfmillar%29Jan2000.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="441" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:LochLomond(wfmillar)Jan2000.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Loch_Lomond" title="Loch Lomond">Loch Lomond</a> from Beinn Dubh and Creag an t-Seilich</div></div></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_freshwater_islands_in_Scotland" title="List of freshwater islands in Scotland">List of freshwater islands in Scotland</a></div>\n<p>There are numerous other freshwater islands, of which the more notable include <a href="/wiki/Lochindorb" title="Lochindorb">Lochindorb Castle Island</a>, <a href="/wiki/Loch_Leven_Castle" title="Loch Leven Castle">Loch Leven Castle Island</a>, <a href="/wiki/St_Serf%27s_Inch" title="St Serf&#39;s Inch">St Serf\'s Inch</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Inchmahome" title="Inchmahome">Inchmahome</a>, each of which have played an important part in Scottish history.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Inchmurrin" title="Inchmurrin">Inchmurrin</a> is the largest freshwater island in the <a href="/wiki/British_Isles" title="British Isles">British Isles</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Dow_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dow-54">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> It is in <a href="/wiki/Loch_Lomond" title="Loch Lomond">Loch Lomond</a>, which contains over sixty other islands.<sup id="cite_ref-Dow_54-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dow-54">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Loch_Maree" title="Loch Maree">Loch Maree</a> also contains several islands, the largest of which are <a href="/wiki/Eilean_S%C3%B9bhainn" title="Eilean S\xc3\xb9bhainn">Eilean S\xc3\xb9bhainn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Garbh_Eilean,_Loch_Maree" title="Garbh Eilean, Loch Maree">Garbh Eilean</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eilean_Ruairidh_M%C3%B2r" title="Eilean Ruairidh M\xc3\xb2r">Eilean Ruairidh M\xc3\xb2r</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Smaller_offshore_islands">Smaller offshore islands</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_islands_of_Scotland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Smaller offshore islands">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>This is a continuing list of uninhabited Scottish islands smaller than 40 hectares in size.\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable archipelagos</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_islands_of_Scotland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: href="/wiki/File:Boreray_and_the_Stacs.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Boreray_and_the_Stacs.jpg/200px-Boreray_and_the_Stacs.jpg" width="200" height="155" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Boreray_and_the_Stacs.jpg/300px-Boreray_and_the_Stacs.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Boreray_and_the_Stacs.jpg/400px-Boreray_and_the_Stacs.jpg 2x" data-file-width="581" data-file-height="451" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Boreray_and_the_Stacs.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Boreray,_St_Kilda" title="Boreray, St Kilda">Boreray</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stac_Lee" title="Stac Lee">Stac Lee</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Stac_an_Armin" title="Stac an Armin">Stac an Armin</a> (left) from the heights of Conachair, <a href="/wiki/St_Kilda,_Scotland" title="St Kilda, Scotland">St Kilda</a></div></div></div>\n<p>There are various small archipelagos which may be better known than the larger islands they contain. class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_islands_of_Scotland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Former islands">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Eilean_Chaluim_Chille_(photo,_2008).jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Eilean_Chaluim_Chille_%28photo%2C_2008%29.jpeg/220px-Eilean_Chaluim_Chille_%28photo%2C_2008%29.jpeg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Eilean_Chaluim_Chille_%28photo%2C_2008%29.jpeg/330px-Eilean_Chaluim_Chille_%28photo%2C_2008%29.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Eilean_Chaluim_Chille_%28photo%2C_2008%29.jpeg/440px-Eilean_Chaluim_Chille_%28photo%2C_2008%29.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="427" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Eilean_Chaluim_Chille_(photo,_2008).jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Ruined ecclesiastical buildings remain visible on Eilean Chaluim Chille, near <a href="/wiki/Kilmuir,_Skye" title="Kilmuir, Skye">Kilmuir</a>, Skye.</div></div></div>\n<p>The following is a list of places which were formerly islands, but which are no longer so due to silting up, harbour building etc.\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scalp_na_Caoraich&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Scalp na Caoraich (page does not exist)">Scalp na Caoraich</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cridhe_An_Uisge&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Cridhe An Uisge (page does not exist)">Cridhe An Uisge</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=R%C3%B2nach&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="R\xc3\xb2nach (page does not exist)">R\xc3\xb2nach</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=%27Scalp_Ph%C3%A0draig_Mh%C3%B2ir&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="&#39;Scalp Ph\xc3\xa0draig Mh\xc3\xb2ir (page does not exist)">\'Scalp Ph\xc3\xa0draig Mh\xc3\xb2ir</a> - four small islands at the delta of the <a href="/wiki/River_Ness" title="River Ness">River Ness</a> in <a href="/wiki/Inverness" title="Inverness">Inverness</a> which were removed in the 19th century.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Broch_of_Clickimin" title="Broch of Clickimin">Broch of Clickimin</a> is a former island in Loch of Clickimin, <a href="/wiki/Lerwick" title="Lerwick">Lerwick</a>, in Shetland. Originally an offshore island, the loch became cut off from the sea around 200 BC and the island is now connected to dry land by a permanent causeway.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>Bunglan was once a separate island, but is now connected to <a href="/wiki/Samphrey" title="Samphrey">Samphrey</a> by two <a href="/wiki/Tombolo" title="Tombolo">tombolos</a>.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Eilean-a-beithich" title="Eilean-a-beithich">Eilean-a-beithich</a> was once one of the <a href="/wiki/Slate_Islands" title="Slate Islands">Slate Islands</a> and located in Easdale Sound. However, it was quarried to a depth of 76 metres (249&#160;ft) below sea level leaving only the outer rim of the island. This was eventually breached by the sea and little visible sign of the island now remains.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>Eilean Chaluim Chille is a former island near <a href="/wiki/Kilmuir,_Skye" title="Kilmuir, Skye">Kilmuir</a> on Skye in a now drained loch that was associated with the 13th century Hebridean lord <a href="/wiki/P%C3%A1ll,_son_of_B%C3%A1lki" class="mw-redirect" title="P\xc3\xa1ll, son of B\xc3\xa1lki">P\xc3\xa1ll, son of B\xc3\xa1lki</a>.</li>\n<li>Inchbroach, also known as Rossie Island, is now part of <a href="/wiki/Montrose,_Angus" title="Montrose, Angus">Montrose</a> harbour.</li>\n<li>Inch of Culter is a former island in the <a href="/wiki/River_Dee,_Aberdeenshire" title="River Dee, Aberdeenshire">River Dee</a> near <a href="/wiki/Maryculter" title="Maryculter">Maryculter</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>Innis Bheag or <a href="/wiki/Paterson_Island" class="mw-redirect" title="Paterson Island">Paterson Island</a> near <a href="/wiki/Portmahomack" title="Portmahomack">Portmahomack</a> in Easter Ross is now permanently attached to the <a href="/wiki/Morrich_More" title="Morrich More">Morrich More</a> due to shifting sands.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Keith_Inch" title="Keith Inch">Keith Inch</a> (not to be confused with <a href="/wiki/Inchkeith" title="Inchkeith">Inchkeith</a>), is now part of <a href="/wiki/Peterhead" title="Peterhead">Peterhead Harbour</a>, and is the <a href="/wiki/Extreme_points_of_the_United_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="Extreme points of the United Kingdom">easternmost point</a> of mainland <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a>.</li>\n<li>King\'s Inch, on which stood <a href="/wiki/Renfrew_Castle" title="Renfrew Castle">Renfrew Castle</a>.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_North_Inch" title="Battle of the North Inch">North Inch</a>, one of the "Inches" in <a href="/wiki/Perth,_Scotland" title="Perth, Scotland">Perth</a>, formerly an island in the <a href="/wiki/River_Tay" title="River Tay">River Tay</a>.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Rosyth_Castle" title="Rosyth Castle">Rosyth Castle</a> also stands on what was once a tidal island in the <a href="/wiki/Firth_of_Forth" title="Firth of Forth">Firth of Forth</a>, now surrounded by reclaimed land.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Preston_Island,_Fife" class="mw-redirect" title="Preston Island, Fife">Preston Island</a>, an artificial construction south of Low Valleyfield, has now been fully reclaimed, using ash slurry from <a href="/wiki/Longannet_power_station" title="Longannet power station">Longannet power station</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Viking_Bergen_Island" title="Viking Bergen Island">Viking Bergen Island</a>, a sunken island of the early <a href="/wiki/Holocene" title="Holocene">Holocene</a>.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Whiteinch" title="Whiteinch">Whiteinch</a>, now an area of <a href="/wiki/Glasgow" title="Glasgow">Glasgow</a>.</li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Bridged_islands">Bridged islands</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_islands_of_Scotland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Bridged islands">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Skye_Road_Bridge.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Skye_Road_Bridge.JPG/200px-Skye_Road_Bridge.JPG" width="200" height="133" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Skye_Road_Bridge.JPG/300px-Skye_Road_Bridge.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Skye_Road_Bridge.JPG/400px-Skye_Road_Bridge.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1500" data-file-height="1000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Skye_Road_Bridge.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Skye_bridge" class="mw-redirect" title="Skye bridge">Skye bridge</a>, <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Skye" class="mw-redirect" title="Isle of Skye">Isle of Skye</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Inchgarvie.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Inchgarvie.JPG/200px-Inchgarvie.JPG" width="200" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Inchgarvie.JPG/300px-Inchgarvie.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Inchgarvie.JPG/400px-Inchgarvie.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1944" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Inchgarvie.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Inchgarvie can be seen just below the <a href="/wiki/Forth_Bridge" title="Forth Bridge">Forth Bridge</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Causeway,_Island_of_Danna_-_geograph.org.uk_-_469472.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Causeway%2C_Island_of_Danna_-_geograph.org.uk_-_469472.jpg/200px-Causeway%2C_Island_of_Danna_-_geograph.org.uk_-_469472.jpg" width="200" height="133" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Causeway%2C_Island_of_Danna_-_geograph.org.uk_-_469472.jpg/300px-Causeway%2C_Island_of_Danna_-_geograph.org.uk_-_469472.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Causeway%2C_Island_of_Danna_-_geograph.org.uk_-_469472.jpg/400px-Causeway%2C_Island_of_Danna_-_geograph.org.uk_-_469472.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="427" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Causeway,_Island_of_Danna_-_geograph.org.uk_-_469472.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The stone causeway to <a href="/wiki/Danna,_Scotland" title="Danna, Scotland">Danna</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Many of Scotland\'s islands are connected to the mainland and/or other islands by bridge or causeway. Although some people consider them no longer to be islands, they are generally treated as such.\n</p><p><b>Outer Hebrides</b>\n</p><p>Many of the islands of the southern Outer Hebrides have been joined to other islands by causeways and bridges. These include:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Baleshare" title="Baleshare">Baleshare</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Benbecula" title="Benbecula">Benbecula</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Berneray,_North_Uist" class="mw-redirect" title="Berneray, North Uist">Berneray</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Eriskay" title="Eriskay">Eriskay</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Grimsay" title="Grimsay">Grimsay</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/North_Uist" title="North Uist">North Uist</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/South_Uist" title="South Uist">South Uist</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Vatersay" title="Vatersay">Vatersay</a>, which joined to <a href="/wiki/Barra" title="Barra">Barra</a>, but not to the above islands.</li></ul>\n<p>To the north, <a href="/wiki/Scalpay,_Outer_Hebrides" title="Scalpay, Outer Hebrides">Scalpay</a> and <a href="/wiki/Great_Bernera" title="Great Bernera">Great Bernera</a> are connected to <a href="/wiki/Lewis_and_Harris" title="Lewis and Harris">Lewis and Harris</a>.\n</p><p><b>Inner Hebrides</b>\n</p>\n<ul><li>The <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Skye" class="mw-redirect" title="Isle of Skye">Isle of Skye</a> is connected to the mainland by the <a href="/wiki/Skye_Bridge" title="Skye Bridge">Skye Bridge</a> which now incorporates <a href="/wiki/Eilean_B%C3%A0n,_Lochalsh" title="Eilean B\xc3\xa0n, Lochalsh">Eilean B\xc3\xa0n</a>.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Eilean_Donan" title="Eilean Donan">Eilean Donan</a> by causeway to the mainland</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Eriska" title="Eriska">Eriska</a> by causeway to the mainland</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Seil" title="Seil">Seil</a> (to mainland) via John Stevenson\'s<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> 1792 "<a href="/wiki/Clachan_Bridge" title="Clachan Bridge">Bridge over The Atlantic</a>".</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Danna,_Scotland" title="Danna, Scotland">Danna</a>  by causeway to the mainland</li></ul>\n<p><b>Orkney Islands</b>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Churchill_Barrier_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Churchill_Barrier_1.jpg/200px-Churchill_Barrier_1.jpg" width="200" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Churchill_Barrier_1.jpg/300px-Churchill_Barrier_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Churchill_Barrier_1.jpg/400px-Churchill_Barrier_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2304" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Churchill_Barrier_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Churchill_Barrier" class="mw-redirect" title="Churchill Barrier">Churchill Barrier</a> 1, blocking Kirk Sound</div></div></div>\n<p>Similarly, four Orkney islands are joined to the <a href="/wiki/Mainland,_Orkney" title="Mainland, Orkney">Orkney Mainland</a> by a series of <a href="/wiki/Causeway" title="Causeway">causeways</a> known as the <a href="/wiki/Churchill_Barriers" title="Churchill Barriers">Churchill Barriers</a>. They are:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/South_Ronaldsay" title="South Ronaldsay">South Ronaldsay</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Burray" title="Burray">Burray</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Lamb_Holm" title="Lamb Holm">Lamb Holm</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Glims_Holm" title="Glims Holm">Glims Holm</a></li></ul>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Hunda" title="Hunda">Hunda</a> is in turn connected to Burray via a causeway.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/South_Walls" title="South Walls">South Walls</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hoy" title="Hoy">Hoy</a> are connected by a causeway called the Ayre. The islands are treated as one entity (Hoy) by the UK census.\n</p><p>An undersea tunnel between the archipelago and <a href="/wiki/Caithness" title="Caithness">Caithness</a>, at a length of about 9\xe2\x80\x9310 miles (14\xe2\x80\x9316&#160;km) and a tunnel connecting Orkney Mainland to Shapinsay have been discussed,<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> although little has come of it.\n</p><p><b>Shetland Islands</b>\n</p><p>Several Shetland islands are joined to the <a href="/wiki/Mainland,_Shetland" title="Mainland, Shetland">Shetland Mainland</a>:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/West_Burra" title="West Burra">West Burra</a> and <a href="/wiki/East_Burra" title="East Burra">East Burra</a> (via Trondra)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Muckle_Roe" title="Muckle Roe">Muckle Roe</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Trondra" title="Trondra">Trondra</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Broch_of_Clickimin" title="Broch of Clickimin">Broch of Clickimin</a> is a freshwater islet joined to the mainland by a stone causeway.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<p>There is also a bridge from <a href="/wiki/Housay" title="Housay">Housay</a> to <a href="/wiki/Bruray" title="Bruray">Bruray</a>.\n</p><p><b>Others</b>\n</p><p>Various other islands are also connected by bridges or causeways, to the mainland or other islands, including:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Inchgarvie" title="Inchgarvie">Inchgarvie</a> (part of <a href="/wiki/Forth_Bridge" title="Forth Bridge">Forth Bridge</a>), thus joined to both <a href="/wiki/Fife" title="Fife">Fife</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lothian" title="Lothian">Lothian</a> on the Mainland.</li>\n<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Garbh_Eilean,_Kylesku&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Garbh Eilean, Kylesku (page does not exist)">Garbh Eilean</a> at the entrance to Loch Glencoul is now joined to the mainland by both the <a href="/wiki/Kylesku_Bridge" title="Kylesku Bridge">Kylesku Bridge</a> to the south and its associated roadworks to the north.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Innis_Chonan" class="mw-redirect" title="Innis Chonan">Innis Chonan</a>, an inhabited island in <a href="/wiki/Loch_Awe" title="Loch Awe">Loch Awe</a> is connected to the mainland by a small road bridge.</li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Tidal_islands_and_tombolos">Tidal islands and tombolos</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_islands_of_Scotland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Tidal islands and tombolos">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Oronsay_-_Hebrides.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Oronsay_-_Hebrides.jpg/200px-Oronsay_-_Hebrides.jpg" width="200" height="120" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Oronsay_-_Hebrides.jpg/300px-Oronsay_-_Hebrides.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Oronsay_-_Hebrides.jpg/400px-Oronsay_-_Hebrides.jpg 2x" data-file-width="630" data-file-height="377" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Oronsay_-_Hebrides.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A beach on <a href="/wiki/Oronsay,_Inner_Hebrides" title="Oronsay, Inner Hebrides">Oronsay</a> by <a href="/wiki/Colonsay" title="Colonsay">Colonsay</a>, looking towards the Paps of <a href="/wiki/Jura,_Scotland" title="Jura, Scotland">Jura</a> in the distance.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:St_Ninian%27s_Isle_and_tombolo.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/St_Ninian%27s_Isle_and_tombolo.jpg/200px-St_Ninian%27s_Isle_and_tombolo.jpg" width="200" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/St_Ninian%27s_Isle_and_tombolo.jpg/300px-St_Ninian%27s_Isle_and_tombolo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/St_Ninian%27s_Isle_and_tombolo.jpg/400px-St_Ninian%27s_Isle_and_tombolo.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="960" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:St_Ninian%27s_Isle_and_tombolo.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/St_Ninian%27s_Isle" title="St Ninian&#39;s Isle">St Ninian\'s Isle</a> and tombolo</div></div></div>\n<p>There are a large number of small <a href="/wiki/Tidal_islands" class="mw-redirect" title="Tidal islands">tidal islands</a> in Scotland. The more notable ones include:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Baleshare" title="Baleshare">Baleshare</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Bernera,_Lismore" title="Bernera, Lismore">Bernera</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Calve_Island" title="Calve Island">Calve Island</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Castle_Island,_Scotland" title="Castle Island, Scotland">Castle Island</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Corn_Holm" title="Corn Holm">Corn Holm</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Cramond_Island" title="Cramond Island">Cramond Island</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Davaar_Island" title="Davaar Island">Davaar Island</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Eilean_Mhic_Chrion" title="Eilean Mhic Chrion">Eilean Mhic Chrion</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Eilean_Shona" title="Eilean Shona">Eilean Shona</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Eriska" title="Eriska">Eriska</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Erraid" title="Erraid">Erraid</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Helliar_Holm" title="Helliar Holm">Helliar Holm</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Kili_Holm" title="Kili Holm">Kili Holm</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Isle_Ristol" title="Isle Ristol">Isle Ristol</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Sanday,_Inner_Hebrides" title="Sanday, Inner Hebrides">Sanday</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Torsa" title="Torsa">Torsa</a></li></ul>\n<p><i>Oronsay</i> means "ebb island" and there are several tidal islands of this name.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The three main islands of the <a href="/wiki/Monach_Islands" title="Monach Islands">Monach Islands</a> (Heisgeir), <a href="/wiki/Ceann_Iar" title="Ceann Iar">Ceann Iar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ceann_Ear" title="Ceann Ear">Ceann Ear</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shivinish" class="mw-redirect" title="Shivinish">Shivinish</a> are connected at low tides. It is said that at one time it was also possible to walk all the way to <a href="/wiki/Baleshare" title="Baleshare">Baleshare</a>, and on to <a href="/wiki/North_Uist" title="North Uist">North Uist</a>, five miles away at low tide. In the 16th century, a large tidal wave was said to have washed the route away.<sup id="cite_ref-Smith_2-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Smith-2">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/St_Ninian%27s_Isle" title="St Ninian&#39;s Isle">St Ninian\'s Isle</a> is connected to <a href="/wiki/Mainland,_Shetland" title="Mainland, Shetland">Mainland Shetland</a> by a <a href="/wiki/Tombolo" title="Tombolo">tombolo</a>. Although greater than 40 hectares in size it fails to meet the definition of an island used in this list as it is only surrounded by water during occasional <a href="/wiki/Spring_tide" class="mw-redirect" title="Spring tide">spring tides</a> and storms.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/D%C3%B9n,_St_Kilda" title="D\xc3\xb9n, St Kilda">D\xc3\xb9n</a> in <a href="/wiki/St_Kilda,_Scotland" title="St Kilda, Scotland">St Kilda</a> is separated from <a href="/wiki/Hirta" title="Hirta">Hirta</a> by a shallow strait about 50 metres wide. This is normally impassable but is reputed to dry out on rare occasions.<sup id="cite_ref-Smith_2-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Smith-2">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Complex_islands">Complex islands</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_islands_of_Scotland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Complex islands">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Eileanan_Chearabhaigh.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Eileanan_Chearabhaigh.jpg/200px-Eileanan_Chearabhaigh.jpg" width="200" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Eileanan_Chearabhaigh.jpg/300px-Eileanan_Chearabhaigh.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Eileanan_Chearabhaigh.jpg/400px-Eileanan_Chearabhaigh.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="3000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Eileanan_Chearabhaigh.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The islands of <a href="/wiki/Eileanan_Chearabhaigh" title="Eileanan Chearabhaigh">Eileanan Chearabhaigh</a> at centre, with mainland <a href="/wiki/Benbecula" title="Benbecula">Benbecula</a> in the foreground and the northern tip of <a href="/wiki/Wiay,_Uist" title="Wiay, Uist">Wiay</a> beyond</div></div></div>\n<p>There are a number of offshore islands that defy easy classification.\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Ceallasaigh_M%C3%B2r" title="Ceallasaigh M\xc3\xb2r">Ceallasaigh M\xc3\xb2r</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ceallasaigh_Beag" title="Ceallasaigh Beag">Ceallasaigh Beag</a> are islands in <a href="/wiki/Lochmaddy" title="Lochmaddy">Loch Maddy</a>, North Uist which are both c. 50 hectares (120 acres) in extent at high tide. At low tide they are connected to one another and several other small tidal islets in the shallow lagoon that surrounds them.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Eileanan_Iasgaich" title="Eileanan Iasgaich">Eileanan Iasgaich</a> in <a href="/wiki/Lochboisdale" title="Lochboisdale">Loch Boisdale</a>, South Uist comprises five small islands and several other islets at high tide but forms a single large one of 50 hectares (120 acres) at low tide.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Eileanan_Chearabhaigh" title="Eileanan Chearabhaigh">Eileanan Chearabhaigh</a>. At low tide these islands form a peninsula with a total area of 49 hectares (120 acres), which is connected to Benbecula by drying sands.<sup id="cite_ref-Rick_47-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rick-47">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> At high tide the connection to Benbecula is lost and a number of small islets stretching for  over  2 kilometres (1.2&#160;mi) from east to west appear, the largest of which is about 30 hectares (74 acres) in extent.</li>\n<li>The Crowlin Islands, located in the <a href="/wiki/Inner_Sound,_Scotland" title="Inner Sound, Scotland">Inner Sound</a> off  Raasay are three separate islands at high tide and a single one of 270 hectares (670 acres) at low tide.</li>\n<li>Similarly, <a href="/wiki/Lunga,_Firth_of_Lorn" class="mw-redirect" title="Lunga, Firth of Lorn">Lunga</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Firth_of_Lorn" title="Firth of Lorn">Firth of Lorn</a> is six or more separate islets at high tide but a single one of 254 hectares (630 acres) at low tide.</li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Castle_islands">Castle islands</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_islands_of_Scotland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Castle islands">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Castle_Stalker_Scotland.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Castle_Stalker_Scotland.jpg/200px-Castle_Stalker_Scotland.jpg" width="200" height="133" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Castle_Stalker_Scotland.jpg/300px-Castle_Stalker_Scotland.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Castle_Stalker_Scotland.jpg/400px-Castle_Stalker_Scotland.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="1996" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Castle_Stalker_Scotland.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Castle Stalker, as seen in <i><a href="/wiki/Monty_Python_and_the_Holy_Grail" title="Monty Python and the Holy Grail">Monty Python and the Holy Grail</a></i></div></div></div>\n<p>There are several small Scottish islands that are dominated by a castle or other fortification. The castle is often better known than the island, and the islands themselves are often tidal or bridged. Due to their picturesque nature some of them are well-known from postcards and films. Examples include:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Bass_Rock" title="Bass Rock">Bass Rock</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Broch_of_West_Burrafirth" title="Broch of West Burrafirth">Broch of West Burrafirth</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Castle_Island,_Scotland" title="Castle Island, Scotland">Castle Island</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Calvay" title="Calvay">Calvay</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Castle_Stalker" title="Castle Stalker">Castle Stalker</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Castle_Tioram" title="Castle Tioram">Castle Tioram</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Eilean_Aigas" title="Eilean Aigas">Eilean Aigas</a> (F)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Eilean_Dearg,_Loch_Riddon" class="mw-redirect" title="Eilean Dearg, Loch Riddon">Eilean Dearg, Loch Riddon</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Eilean_Donan" title="Eilean Donan">Eilean Donan</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Inchtalla" title="Inchtalla">Inchtalla</a> (F)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Inveruglas_Isle" title="Inveruglas Isle">Inveruglas Isle</a> (F)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Kilchurn_Castle" title="Kilchurn Castle">Kilchurn Castle</a> (F)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Kisimul_Castle" title="Kisimul Castle">Kisimul Castle</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Lochindorb" title="Lochindorb">Lochindorb Castle</a> (F)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Loch_Leven_Castle" title="Loch Leven Castle">Loch Leven Castle</a> (F)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Mousa" title="Mousa">Mousa</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Threave_Castle" title="Threave Castle">Threave Castle</a> (F)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Wyre,_Orkney" title="Wyre, Orkney">Wyre</a></li></ul>\n<p>Many of the <a href="/wiki/Islands_of_the_Forth" title="Islands of the Forth">Islands of the Forth</a> and southern <a href="/wiki/Orkney" title="Orkney">Orkneys</a> have fortifications from the two world wars. <a href="/wiki/Rosyth_Castle" title="Rosyth Castle">Rosyth Castle</a> stands on a former island.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Holy_islands">Holy islands</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_islands_of_Scotland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Holy islands">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Centre_for_world_peace_on_holy_isle_with_flags.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Centre_for_world_peace_on_holy_isle_with_flags.jpg/200px-Centre_for_world_peace_on_holy_isle_with_flags.jpg" width="200" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Centre_for_world_peace_on_holy_isle_with_flags.jpg/300px-Centre_for_world_peace_on_holy_isle_with_flags.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Centre_for_world_peace_on_holy_isle_with_flags.jpg/400px-Centre_for_world_peace_on_holy_isle_with_flags.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="600" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Centre_for_world_peace_on_holy_isle_with_flags.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Tibetan Buddhist Centre for World Peace and Health on Holy Isle</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Oransay_Priory.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Oransay_Priory.JPG/200px-Oransay_Priory.JPG" width="200" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Oransay_Priory.JPG/300px-Oransay_Priory.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Oransay_Priory.JPG/400px-Oransay_Priory.JPG 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Oransay_Priory.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Oronsay Priory</div></div></div>\n<p>A huge number of the islands of Scotland have some kind of <a href="/wiki/Culdee" class="mw-redirect" title="Culdee">culdee</a>/church connection, and/or are dominated by a church. The more notable include:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Davaar_Island" title="Davaar Island">Davaar Island</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Egilsay" title="Egilsay">Egilsay</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Eynhallow" title="Eynhallow">Eynhallow</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Holy_Isle,_Firth_of_Clyde" title="Holy Isle, Firth of Clyde">Holy Isle</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Inchcolm" title="Inchcolm">Inchcolm</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Inch_Kenneth" title="Inch Kenneth">Inch Kenneth</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Inchmahome" title="Inchmahome">Inchmahome</a> (F)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Iona" title="Iona">Iona</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Isle_Maree" title="Isle Maree">Isle Maree</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/North_Rona" title="North Rona">North Rona</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Oronsay,_Inner_Hebrides" title="Oronsay, Inner Hebrides">Oronsay</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Papa_Stronsay" title="Papa Stronsay">Papa Stronsay</a> (current <a href="/wiki/Transalpine_Redemptorist" class="mw-redirect" title="Transalpine Redemptorist">Transalpine Redemptorist</a> monastery. Islands called "Papa" or "Pabbay" tend to be former saints\' islands)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/St_Ninian%27s_Isle" title="St Ninian&#39;s Isle">St Ninian\'s Isle</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/St_Serf%27s_Inch" title="St Serf&#39;s Inch">St Serf\'s Inch</a> (F)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Tiree" title="Tiree">Tiree</a> ("land of Iona")</li></ul>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Brother_Isle" title="Brother Isle">Brother Isle</a>\'s name is not ecclesiastical in origin as is sometimes stated.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Islands_named_after_people">Islands named after people</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_islands_of_Scotland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Islands named after people">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>This is a list of islands, which are known to be named after someone. In some cases such as <a href="/wiki/North_Ronaldsay" title="North Ronaldsay">North Ronaldsay</a> this status may not be obvious (it isn\'t named after a "Ronald", unlike <a href="/wiki/South_Ronaldsay" title="South Ronaldsay">South Ronaldsay</a>). This list omits names such as <a href="/wiki/Hildasay" title="Hildasay">Hildasay</a>, where the person in question is mythological, or <a href="/wiki/Ailsa_Craig" title="Ailsa Craig">Ailsa Craig</a>, where the individual in question is not known, and also <a href="/wiki/Colonsay" title="Colonsay">Colonsay</a> &amp; <a href="/wiki/Egilsay" title="Egilsay">Egilsay</a> where the derivation is disputed.\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Eilean_Chaluim_Chille" title="Eilean Chaluim Chille">Eilean Chaluim Chille</a> - <a href="/wiki/Saint_Columba" class="mw-redirect" title="Saint Columba">Saint Columba</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Davaar_Island" title="Davaar Island">Island Davaar</a> - Saint Barr</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Eilean_Donan" title="Eilean Donan">Eilean Donan</a>  - <a href="/wiki/Saint_Donan" class="mw-redirect" title="Saint Donan">Saint Donan</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Flannan_Isles" title="Flannan Isles">Flannan Isles</a> - <a href="/wiki/Saint_Flannan" class="mw-redirect" title="Saint Flannan">Saint Flannan</a></li>\n<li>Frank Lockwood\'s Island (south of <a href="/wiki/Lochbuie,_Mull" title="Lochbuie, Mull">Lochbuie, Mull</a>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Inchcolm" title="Inchcolm">Inchcolm</a>  - <a href="/wiki/Saint_Columba" class="mw-redirect" title="Saint Columba">Saint Columba</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Inch_Kenneth" title="Inch Kenneth">Inch Kenneth</a>  - <a href="/wiki/Saint_Kenneth" class="mw-redirect" title="Saint Kenneth">Saint Kenneth</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Inchmarnock" title="Inchmarnock">Inchmarnock</a> - Saint Mearnag</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Inchmahome" title="Inchmahome">Inchmahome</a> (F) - Saint Colmag</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Inchmurrin" title="Inchmurrin">Inchmurrin</a> (F) - Saint Meadhran/Mirin</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Innis_Chonan" class="mw-redirect" title="Innis Chonan">Innis Chonan</a> (F) - <a href="/wiki/Saint_Conan" title="Saint Conan">Saint Conan</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Isle_Maree" title="Isle Maree">Isle Maree</a> (F) - Maelrubha</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Isle_Martin" title="Isle Martin">Isle Martin</a>  - <a href="/wiki/Martin_of_Tours" title="Martin of Tours">Saint Martin</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/North_Rona" title="North Rona">North Rona</a> - <a href="/wiki/Saint_Ronan" class="mw-redirect" title="Saint Ronan">Saint Ronan</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/St_Serf%27s_Inch" title="St Serf&#39;s Inch">St Serf\'s Inch</a> (F) - <a href="/wiki/Saint_Serf" title="Saint Serf">Saint Serf</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Sweyn_Holm" title="Sweyn Holm">Sweyn Holm</a> \xe2\x80\x93 <a href="/wiki/Sweyn_Asleifsson" title="Sweyn Asleifsson">Sweyn Asleifsson</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Taransay" title="Taransay">Taransay</a> - <a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Taran&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Saint Taran (page does not exist)">Saint Taran</a></li></ul>\n<p>Iqbal Singh, the owner of <a href="/wiki/Vacsay" title="Vacsay">Vacsay</a>, has also expressed wishes to rename it after <a href="/wiki/Robert_Burns" title="Robert Burns">Robert Burns</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span id="Places_called_.22island.22_etc._that_are_not_islands"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Places_called_&quot;island&quot;_etc._that_are_not_islands">Places called "island" etc. that are not islands</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_islands_of_Scotland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Places called &quot;island&quot; etc. that are not islands">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Burntisland_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Burntisland_1.jpg/200px-Burntisland_1.jpg" width="200" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Burntisland_1.jpg/300px-Burntisland_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Burntisland_1.jpg/400px-Burntisland_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Burntisland_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Burntisland - not actually an island</div></div></div>\n<p>Some places in Scotland with names including "isle" or "island" are not islands. They include:\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable sortable">\n<caption>\n</caption>\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Name\n</th>\n<th>Island group / location\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Black_Isle" title="Black Isle">Black Isle</a> (<i>An t-Eilean Dubh</i>)\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Ross_and_Cromarty" title="Ross and Cromarty">Ross and Cromarty</a>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Burntisland" title="Burntisland">Burntisland</a>\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Fife" title="Fife">Fife</a>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gluss_Isle&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Gluss Isle (page does not exist)">Gluss Isle</a>\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Shetland" title="Shetland">Shetland</a>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Harris" class="mw-redirect" title="Isle of Harris">Isle of Harris</a> (<i>Na Hearadh</i>)\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Outer_Hebrides" title="Outer Hebrides">Outer Hebrides</a>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Lewis" title="Isle of Lewis">Isle of Lewis</a> (<i>Eilean Le\xc3\xb2dhais</i>)\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Outer_Hebrides" title="Outer Hebrides">Outer Hebrides</a>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Isleornsay" title="Isleornsay">Isleornsay</a> (<i>Eilean Iarmain</i>)\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Skye" title="Skye">Skye</a>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Islesteps (south of <a href="/wiki/Dumfries" title="Dumfries">Dumfries</a>)\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Dumfries_and_Galloway" title="Dumfries and Galloway">Dumfries and Galloway</a>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Whithorn" title="Isle of Whithorn">Isle of Whithorn</a>\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Dumfries_and_Galloway" title="Dumfries and Galloway">Dumfries and Galloway</a>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>Lewis and Harris are separated by a range of hills but form one island, and are sometimes referred to as "<a href="/wiki/Lewis_and_Harris" title="Lewis and Harris">Lewis and Harris</a>". Isle of Whithorn and the Black Isle are peninsulas, and Isleornsay is a village which looks out onto the island of <a href="/wiki/Ornsay" title="Ornsay">Ornsay</a>. There is no commonly accepted derivation for "Burntisland" which had numerous other forms in the past, such as "Brintilun" and "Ye Brint Eland".<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Gluss Isle at the western entrance to <a href="/wiki/Sullom_Voe" title="Sullom Voe">Sullom Voe</a> is one of the many promontories in Orkney and Shetland connected to a larger body of land by an <a href="/wiki/Ayre_(landform)" title="Ayre (landform)">ayre</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_elements">Other elements</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_islands_of_Scotland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Other elements">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Vementry.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Vementry.jpg/200px-Vementry.jpg" width="200" height="136" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Vementry.jpg/300px-Vementry.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Vementry.jpg/400px-Vementry.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="436" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Vementry.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Vementry" title="Vementry">Vementry</a> Farm, on Mainland Shetland, with Isle of Vementry in hinterground</div></div></div>\n<p>The name "Inch" (<i>Innis</i>) can mean island (e.g. <a href="/wiki/Inchkenneth" class="mw-redirect" title="Inchkenneth">Inchkenneth</a>, <a href="/wiki/Inchcolm" title="Inchcolm">Inchcolm</a>), but is also used for <i>terra firma</i> surrounded by marsh e.g. <a href="/wiki/Markinch" title="Markinch">Markinch</a>, <a href="/wiki/Insch" title="Insch">Insch</a>.\n</p><p><i>Eilean</i> is <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Gaelic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Scottish Gaelic language">Gaelic</a> for "island". However, Inistrynich, Eilean na Maodail, Eilean Dubh and Liever Island are all <a href="/wiki/Promontory" title="Promontory">promontories</a> on <a href="/wiki/Loch_Awe" title="Loch Awe">Loch Awe</a> as opposed to islands, despite their names. Likewise <a href="/w/index.php?title=Eilean_Aoidhe&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Eilean Aoidhe (page does not exist)">Eilean Aoidhe</a> on <a href="/wiki/Loch_Fyne" title="Loch Fyne">Loch Fyne</a>. The Black Isle is also <i>An t-Eilean Dubh</i> in Gaelic, while <a href="/wiki/Eilean_Glas,_Scalpay" title="Eilean Glas, Scalpay">Eilean Glas</a> is part of Scalpay.\n</p><p>"-holm" is also common as a suffix in various landlocked placenames, especially in the far south of mainland Scotland e.g. <a href="/wiki/Langholm" title="Langholm">Langholm</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kirk_Yetholm" title="Kirk Yetholm">Kirk Yetholm</a>, Holmhead (by <a href="/wiki/Cumnock" title="Cumnock">Cumnock</a>), Holmhill (next to <a href="/wiki/Thornhill,_Dumfries_and_Galloway" title="Thornhill, Dumfries and Galloway">Thornhill</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nithsdale" title="Nithsdale">Nithsdale</a>). Some of these were river islands in their time, or dry land surrounded by marsh. "Holm" can be found in an element in Holmsgarth, now a suburb of <a href="/wiki/Lerwick" title="Lerwick">Lerwick</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Holm,_Mainland_Orkney" class="mw-redirect" title="Holm, Mainland Orkney">Parish of Holm</a> on <a href="/wiki/Mainland,_Shetland" title="Mainland, Shetland">Mainland Shetland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mainland,_Orkney" title="Mainland, Orkney">Mainland Orkney</a> respectively. Neither of these is an island in its own right.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Islands_named_after_mainland_areas">Islands named after mainland areas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_islands_of_Scotland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Islands named after mainland areas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Likewise, occasionally an island may be named after a location on the nearby mainland, or a major neighbouring island - or vice versa. Examples of this include: <a href="/wiki/Vementry" title="Vementry">Vementry</a>, which was originally the name of an island, but whose name has been transferred to a nearby farm on Mainland Shetland; <a href="/wiki/Oldany_Island" title="Oldany Island">Oldany Island</a>, whose name has been transferred to <a href="/w/index.php?title=Oldany&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Oldany (page does not exist)">Oldany</a>; <a href="/wiki/Cramond_Island" title="Cramond Island">Cramond Island</a> which is named after neighbouring <a href="/wiki/Cramond" title="Cramond">Cramond</a> (a district of <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh" title="Edinburgh">Edinburgh</a>); and <a href="/wiki/Eilean_Mhealasta" title="Eilean Mhealasta">Eilean Mhealasta</a> in the Outer Hebrides, which is named after <a href="/wiki/Mealista" title="Mealista">Mealista</a> on Lewis.\n</p>\n<h2><span id="Crann.C3.B3gs"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Crann\xc3\xb3gs">Crann\xc3\xb3gs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_islands_of_Scotland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Crann\xc3\xb3gs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Loch_tay_crannog_02.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Loch_tay_crannog_02.jpg/200px-Loch_tay_crannog_02.jpg" width="200" height="267" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Loch_tay_crannog_02.jpg/300px-Loch_tay_crannog_02.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Loch_tay_crannog_02.jpg/400px-Loch_tay_crannog_02.jpg 2x" data-file-width="768" data-file-height="1024" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Loch_tay_crannog_02.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Modern reconstruction of a crann\xc3\xb3g in <a href="/wiki/Loch_Tay" title="Loch Tay">Loch Tay</a></div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Crann%C3%B3g" class="mw-redirect" title="Crann\xc3\xb3g">Crann\xc3\xb3gs</a> are <a href="/wiki/Prehistory" title="Prehistory">prehistoric</a> artificial islands created in lochs. There are several hundred sites in Scotland. Today, crann\xc3\xb3gs typically appear as small, circular islands, between 10\xe2\x80\x9330 metres (30\xe2\x80\x9390&#160;feet)  in diameter.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> Scottish examples include:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Breachacha_crannog" title="Breachacha crannog">Breachacha</a> on Coll</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Cherry_Island_(Loch_Ness)" title="Cherry Island (Loch Ness)">Cherry Island</a> in Loch Ness</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/D%C3%B9n_Anlaimh" title="D\xc3\xb9n Anlaimh">D\xc3\xb9n Anlaimh</a> on Coll</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Eilean_D%C3%B2mhnuill" title="Eilean D\xc3\xb2mhnuill">Eilean D\xc3\xb2mhnuill</a> on North Uist</li>\n<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Keppinch&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Keppinch (page does not exist)">Keppinch</a> (or The Kitchen) in Loch Lomond</li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Inchcolm_Abbey.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Inchcolm" title="Inchcolm">Inchcolm</a> Abbey, <a href="/wiki/Firth_of_Forth"
