area</a></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References_and_footnotes">References and footnotes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_islands_of_Scotland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: References and footnotes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p><b>Notes</b>\n</p>\n<div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em; list-style-type: decimal;">\n<ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-1">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Various other definitions are used. For example the General Register Office for Scotland define an island as "a mass of land surrounded by water, separate from the Scottish mainland" but although they include islands linked by bridges etc. this is not clear from this definition. Haswell-Smith (2004) uses "an Island is a piece of land or group of pieces of land which is entirely surrounded by water at Lowest Astronomical Tide and to which there is no permanent means of dry access". This is widely agreed to be unhelpful as it excludes bridged islands. However, the large numbers of small tidal islets essentially defy categorisation.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-14"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-14">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The evidence of maps, sources and photographs makes it clear that <a href="/wiki/South_Walls" title="South Walls">South Walls</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eriska" title="Eriska">Eriska</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fraoch-eilean" class="mw-redirect" title="Fraoch-eilean">Fraoch-eilean</a> are permanently inhabited. These three are tidal islands, although other similar islands are listed. The freshwater islands of <a href="/wiki/Eilean_Aigas" title="Eilean Aigas">Eilean Aigas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Contin_Island" title="Contin Island">Contin Island</a> are also omitted.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-32"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-32">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">For a discussion of some of the factors involved see Coull (1967).</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-43"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-43">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Island areas indicated with an asterisk are estimates based on <a href="/wiki/Ordnance_Survey" title="Ordnance Survey">Ordnance Survey</a> maps and General Register Office for Scotland statistics.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-44"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-44">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Islands classified as inhabited in the 2001 census but not in 2011, and by implication classified as occasionally inhabited, are indicated with a degree symbol \xc2\xb0.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-49"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-49">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">This island has a hotel<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> but the census does not refer to the island at all.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-50"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-50">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">This island is at (<a href="/wiki/Ordnance_Survey_National_Grid" title="Ordnance Survey National Grid">grid reference</a> <span style="white-space: nowrap" class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="https://tools.wmflabs.org/os/coor_g/?pagename=List_of_islands_of_Scotland&amp;params=NF860580%29_region%3AGB_scale%3A25000">NF860580)</a></span> and the evidence of both Ordnance Survey maps and photographs (e.g. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.geograph.org.uk/photo/445166">"Houses on Seana Bhaile"</a> Geograph. Retrieved 10 August 2009) indicates a resident population. There is even a name, "Seana Bhaile" for the main settlement. However, neither the census nor the main reference work (Haswell-Smith 2004) refer to the island at all. Its small population is presumably included in nearby Grimsay (which has a population of over 800) by the census.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-52"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-52">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Referred to by the National Records of Scotland (2013) as "Inchruin", which is presumably a typographical error.</span>\n</li>\n</ol></div>\n<p><b>Specific references</b>\n</p>\n<div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em; list-style-type: decimal;">\n<ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-Smith-2"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Smith_2-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Smith_2-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Smith_2-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Smith_2-3"><sup><i><b>d</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Smith_2-4"><sup><i><b>e</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Smith_2-5"><sup><i><b>f</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite id="CITEREFHaswell-Smith2004" class="citation book">Haswell-Smith, Hamish (2004). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.co.uk/books?id=bXFwKl5gVqwC"><i>The Scottish Islands</i></a>.
